<div id="review_82995011" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/82995011" />
    <a title="Matthew Herring" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2427815-matthew-herring"><img alt="Matthew Herring" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1245273874p2/2427815.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/82995011?book_show_action=true">Jan 02, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Matthew Herring" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Matthew Herring" href="/user/show/2427815-matthew-herring">Matthew Herring</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781846054747" href="/book/show/6438404-witch-wizard">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer82995011" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9380833529593113380">I'm beginning to think that James Patterson is just farming out his name and writing format to lesser authors in need of exposure. <i>Witch and Wizard</i> is a serviceable if depressing teen thriller, but the problem starts at the beginning of the novel: the action takes precedence over character development, so the reader never gets a full picture of our protagonists beyond a few snide comments and stress based dialogue. There is allusion to the differences between the siblings, told through the voice</span>
  <span id="freeText9380833529593113380" style="display:none">I'm beginning to think that James Patterson is just farming out his name and writing format to lesser authors in need of exposure. <i>Witch and Wizard</i> is a serviceable if depressing teen thriller, but the problem starts at the beginning of the novel: the action takes precedence over character development, so the reader never gets a full picture of our protagonists beyond a few snide comments and stress based dialogue. There is allusion to the differences between the siblings, told through the voice of whichever character is currently telling the story, but they are largely undefined. The story also takes a while to get to a place you'd want your mind to be. Evil adults are by and large the henchmen, with a mysterious Big Bad whose motives are threadbare, based largely on prophesy and power-madness. And of course there are the obligatory child informants, snotty little SS underlings who tattle to authority in the old Nazi tradition. This story has been told before, and much better. I give it three stars only because it's far from the worst thing I've read from the Patterson/whomever library, and better than Twilight.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9380833529593113380" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1787106251" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17449326477291086398">This book is about a brother and sister named Whit and Wisty Allgood who wake up as wanted criminals who are accused of being a wizard and a witch. The One who is the One (who is the most powerful wizard in the world) has taken over the government and made himself the ruler. He is a ruthless killing machine and he wants to take control of all of the wizards in the world. The One who is the One is now sending all his forces after Whit and Wisty. Can they successfully hide from him? Find out when </span>
  <span id="freeText17449326477291086398" style="display:none">This book is about a brother and sister named Whit and Wisty Allgood who wake up as wanted criminals who are accused of being a wizard and a witch. The One who is the One (who is the most powerful wizard in the world) has taken over the government and made himself the ruler. He is a ruthless killing machine and he wants to take control of all of the wizards in the world. The One who is the One is now sending all his forces after Whit and Wisty. Can they successfully hide from him? Find out when you read this pretty good series. This book made me feel angry, happy, sad, anxious,etc. I liked it when they used their magic to fight off people who were chasing them. I didn't like the parts where there is no action/adventure going on. If you like action/adventure, suspense, and mystery I recommend this book to you. If you have read the <i> Harry Potter Series </i> you would probably like this book.</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tom Mueller" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tom Mueller" href="/user/show/2458751-tom-mueller">Tom Mueller</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audio CD 9781600247729" href="/book/show/6712679-witch-wizard">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2458751-tom-mueller?shelf=notfinished">notfinished</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2458751-tom-mueller?shelf=scifi">scifi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2458751-tom-mueller?shelf=cd-edition">cd-edition</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer439717135" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer675141530287711391">In an attempt at fairness to the "author", I listened to the first of several discs, but had to force myself to get through that. While stopping short of plagiarism, this work offered nothing new. Themes and characters were rehashed from the works of Orwell's 1984, Ursula LeGuin, Bradbury, J.K. Rowlings and no doubt others. I heard nothing new. Far too many original works are left to be read; I gave this one more time than it deserved.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17250997729280240961">This was cute and funny and I enjoyed the audio. It seemed geared towards young teens, with puns on popular brands and an easy to follow plot. Wisty and Whit are cute siblings, they get along and care a lot for each other. The world was interesting and I would like more information about how it got the way it did, with The New Order in charge and "The One" their leader. <br/>The back and forth between siblings was nice and helped move the plot along. I will read the sequel to see what happens with th</span>
  <span id="freeText17250997729280240961" style="display:none">This was cute and funny and I enjoyed the audio. It seemed geared towards young teens, with puns on popular brands and an easy to follow plot. Wisty and Whit are cute siblings, they get along and care a lot for each other. The world was interesting and I would like more information about how it got the way it did, with The New Order in charge and "The One" their leader. <br />The back and forth between siblings was nice and helped move the plot along. I will read the sequel to see what happens with the story. </span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('id4o+bWvEukNT9/Ah7L7HOaFP0XVUcdL2+jyFis1tD6z+EErDvHbgapka6FwR/HDMNrYjRvcSSyAlrSn5nZGpA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('gfrsPcKG7eWxTWDvvhRhLX976YE9VUqdRw16hmeBvea73IXvedgkjRZm1I5J4WvyqSQOSfPYxPocczw3qsJPfA==')})
  }
//]]>

A timely, crucial, and empowering exploration of racism--and antiracism--in America \n\nThis is NOT a history book. This is a book about the here and now. A book to help us better understand why we are where we are. A book about race.\n\nThe construct of race has always been used to gain and keep power, to create dynamics that separate and silence. This remarkable reimagining of Dr. Ibram X. Kendi\'s National Book Award-winning Stamped from the Beginning reveals the history of racist ideas in America, and inspires hope for an antiracist future. It takes you on a race journey from then to now, shows you why we feel how we feel, and why the poison of racism lingers. It also proves that while racist ideas have always been easy to fabricate and distribute, they can also be discredited.\n\nThrough a gripping, fast-paced, and energizing narrative written by beloved award-winner Jason Reynolds, this book shines a light on the many insidious forms of racist ideas--and on ways readers can identify and stamp out racist thoughts in their daily lives.<\/span>\n  <a       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/3780.James_Patterson">About James Patterson</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer13120616521458194195"><a href='http://www.jamespatterson.com' rel='nofollow noopener'>Official US Site</a><br/><a href='http://www.jamespatterson.co.uk' rel='nofollow noopener'>Official UK Site</a><br/><a href='http://jimmypatterson.org' rel='nofollow noopener'>JIMMY Patterson Books</a><br/><a href='http://readkiddoread.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>ReadKiddoRead</a><br/><br/><br/><br/>James Patterson is the world’s bestselling author and most trusted storyteller. He has created more enduring fictional characters than any other novelist writing today, with his Alex Cross, Michael Bennett, Women’s Murder Club, Private, NYPD Red, Daniel X, Maximum Ride, and Middle School series. He has sold over 380 million books wo</span>
  <span id="freeText13120616521458194195" style="display:none"><a href="http://www.jamespatterson.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Official US Site</a><br /><a href="http://www.jamespatterson.co.uk" rel="nofollow noopener">Official UK Site</a><br /><a href="http://jimmypatterson.org" rel="nofollow noopener">JIMMY Patterson Books</a><br /><a href="http://readkiddoread.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">ReadKiddoRead</a><br /><br /><br /><br />James Patterson is the world’s bestselling author and most trusted storyteller. He has created more enduring fictional characters than any other novelist writing today, with his Alex Cross, Michael Bennett, Women’s Murder Club, Private, NYPD Red, Daniel X, Maximum Ride, and Middle School series. He has sold over 380 million books worldwide and currently holds the Guinness World Record for the most #1 New York Times bestsellers. In addition to writing the thriller novels for which he is best known, among them The President Is Missing with President Bill Clinton, Patterson also writes fiction for young readers of all ages, including the Max Einstein series, produced in partnership with the Albert Einstein Estate. He is also the first author to have #1 new titles simultaneously on the New York Times adult and children’s bestseller lists.<br /> <br />The son of an insurance salesman and a schoolteacher, Patterson grew up in Newburgh, New York, and began casually writing at the age of nineteen. In 1969, he graduated from Manhattan College. He was given a full-ride scholarship to Vanderbilt University’s graduate program in English. He left Vanderbilt before getting his PhD due to complications involving the Vietnam War. <br /> <br />Instead, he moved to New York to become a junior copywriter for the advertising agency J. Walter Thompson, eventually becoming CEO of its North American company.<br /> <br />In 1976, while still working for J. Walter Thompson, Patterson published his first novel, The Thomas Berryman Number, with Little, Brown and Company. After being turned down by thirty-one publishers, it won the Edgar Award for Best First Novel. Patterson’s 1993 novel, Along Came a Spider, his first book to feature Alex Cross, was also his first New York Times bestseller in fiction.<br /> <br />In 2001, Morgan Freeman starred as Alex Cross in a film adaptation of Along Came a Spider, and Tyler Perry also played the character in the 2012 film Alex Cross. A film adaptation of Patterson’s middle-grade novel Middle School: The Worst Years of My Life was released in theaters in October 2016.<br /> <br />James Patterson has donated more than one million books to students, focusing on some of the most under-resourced schools and youth programs in the country. To date, he has donated $7.25 million to school and classroom libraries throughout the United States, and $2.1 million to independent bookstores and employees.<br /> <br />Patterson has recently donated over $35 million to his and his wife’s alma maters—the University of Wisconsin, Vanderbilt University, and Manhattan College—and he has established over four hundred Teacher and Writer Education Scholarships at twenty-one colleges and universities throughout the country. Patterson has also donated more than one million books to U.S. soldiers at home and overseas.<br /> <br />In May 2015, Patterson launched a children’s book imprint at Little, Brown—JIMMY Patterson—that is unwaveringly focused on one goal: turning kids into lifelong readers. This imprint also provides resources, strategies, and programs to serve teachers, parents, librarians, and booksellers. Patterson invests proceeds from the sales of JIMMY Patterson Books in pro-reading initiatives.<br /> <br />Patterson also founded ReadKiddoRead.com, a website designed to help parents, teachers, and librarians ignite a new generation’s excitement for reading. Awarded the National Book Foundation’s Innovations in Reading Prize and the American Library Association’s Great Websites for Kids, the site features thoughtful book reviews from a variety of genres and age ranges, a large and lively Facebook community, and contributions from other authors.<br /> <br />Patterson’s awards for adult and children’s literature include the Edgar Award, the International </span>
  <a data-text-id="13120616521458194195" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
